## Turn 38
### Query
how to increase the accuracy of the answers and make it more informative?

### Answer
You can improve answer quality at three levels: data, retrieval, and LLM prompt/parameters.


Add high‑quality guidelines: BTS, ERS, ATS, GOLD, GINA, WHO TB, major review articles.  
Avoid noisy textbooks/board-review PDFs for core guideline questions; they dilute signal.  
Prefer clean digital PDFs over scanned images for better extraction; fix any files that showed lots of OCR warnings during build.  

If a guideline is missing, the model can’t answer it, no matter how good the retrieval is.



In main_resp_ai_The_Final_Version.py, where you create the retriever:
retriever = store.as_retriever(
    search_type="similarity",
    search_kwargs={"k": 10}
)

You can:

1. Increase k to capture more relevant chunks (at the cost of slightly more context noise):
retriever = store.as_retriever(
    search_type="similarity",
    search_kwargs={"k": 20}
)

2. Use MMR (diversity) to avoid many near‑duplicate chunks:
retriever = store.as_retriever(
    search_type="mmr",
    search_kwargs={"k": 20, "fetch_k": 50, "lambda_mult": 0.5}
)

3. Make sure you pass enough context to the LLM:

Right now you join all retrieved contents:
context = "\n\n".join(d.page_content for d in docs)

That’s okay, but you can hard‑limit the total characters to avoid over‑long prompts:
max_chars = 15000
context = ""
for d in docs:
    if len(context) + len(d.page_content) > max_chars:
        break
    context += "\n\n" + d.page_content

This gives the model a focused, but rich set of chunks.



Your current prompt already tells it not to hallucinate. To increase informativeness and structure, adjust the template in main():

Locate:
prompt = PromptTemplate(
    template=(
        "You are an expert pulmonologist AI.\n"
        "Task: Provide a concise, evidence-based answer to the question using ONLY the provided context.\n"
        "Requirements:\n"
        "- Cite each fact by chunk source (e.g., \"[source.pdf, page X]\").\n"
        "- Do not introduce information not covered in the context.\n"
        "- If context lacks an answer, state: \"Insufficient data in provided materials.\"\n\n"
        "Context:\n{context}\n\n"
        "Question:\n{question}\n\n"
        "Answer:\nAnswer without revealing your internal reasoning."
    ),
    input_variables=["context", "question"]
)

Replace with something like:
prompt = PromptTemplate(
    template=(
        "You are an expert pulmonologist AI assistant.\n"
        "Use ONLY the information in the provided context to answer.\n\n"
        "Instructions:\n"
        "1. Start with a 1–3 sentence direct answer.\n"
        "2. Then, if the context allows, add brief bullet points for:\n"
        "   - Key recommendations\n"
        "   - Important thresholds / cutoffs\n"
        "   - When to admit, escalate, or refer\n"
        "3. Cite each important statement with its source file name "
        "   (e.g. \"[source.pdf, pX]\").\n"
        "4. If the context does NOT clearly answer, say exactly: "
        "\"Insufficient data in provided materials.\" and nothing more.\n"
        "5. Do NOT use any information outside the context.\n\n"
        "Context:\n{context}\n\n"
        "Question:\n{question}\n\n"
        "Answer:\nAnswer without revealing your internal reasoning."
    ),
    input_variables=["context", "question"]
)

This tends to give:
Clear top‑line answer.  
Short, structured bullets (more informative).  
Still respects “no hallucination”.



When you create the LLM:
llm = Ollama(model=OLLAMA_MODEL, temperature=0.0, max_tokens=256)

You can:
Increase max_tokens to allow more detail, e.g. 512–768:
llm = Ollama(model=OLLAMA_MODEL, temperature=0.0, max_tokens=512)
Keep temperature=0.0 for deterministic, guideline‑like answers.



For high‑accuracy clinical answers, phrasing helps. Instead of:

> “what are the guidelines for pleural effusion?”

Use:
“According to the British Thoracic Society pleural disease guideline, what are the indications for pleural fluid drainage?”  
“In malignant pleural effusion, what does the ERS or ATS guideline recommend for initial management options?”  

This makes retrieval hit the right chunks and answers more specific and useful.



If you paste your current prompt and retriever block from main_resp_ai_The_Final_Version.py, I can give you a ready‑to‑paste upgraded version tuned specifically for your app.

## Turn 39
### Query
where to put this piece: 
max_chars = 15000
context = ""
for d in docs:
    if len(context) + len(d.page_content) > max_chars:
        break
    context += "\n\n" + d.page_content

### Answer
Put it right after you call the retriever and get docs, replacing your current simple .join().

In main_resp_ai_The_Final_Version.py, you currently have something like:
if query and search:

    store = Chroma(persist_directory=DB_DIR, embedding_function=embeddings)
    retriever = store.as_retriever(search_type="similarity", search_kwargs={"k": 10})
    docs = retriever.invoke(query)

    context = "\n\n".join(d.page_content for d in docs)   # ← REPLACE THIS PART

Change it to:
if query and search:
    embeddings = HuggingFaceEmbeddings(
        model_name=EMBED_MODEL,
        model_kwargs={"device": "cpu"}  # if you added this
    )
    store = Chroma(persist_directory=DB_DIR, embedding_function=embeddings)
    retriever = store.as_retriever(search_type="similarity", search_kwargs={"k": 20})
    docs = retriever.invoke(query)

    # Limit total context length
    max_chars = 15000
    context = ""
    for d in docs:
        if len(context) + len(d.page_content) > max_chars:
            break
        context += "\n\n" + d.page_content

Then the context variable is passed into your PromptTemplate as before:
prompt = PromptTemplate(...).format(context=context, question=query)

"""
main_resp_ai_The_Final_Version.py — Respiratory AI Assistant with improved UI and build progress feedback


cd D:\Dev\Active\RespAI_Project

streamlit run main_resp_ai_The_Final_Version.py

pytesseract.pytesseract.tesseract_cmd = r'C:\Program Files\Tesseract-OCR\tesseract.exe'

# --------------------------------------------------------

def ensure_dir(path: str):
    os.makedirs(path, exist_ok=True)


def file_hash(path: str) -> str:
    h = hashlib.md5()
    with open(path, "rb") as f:
        for chunk in iter(lambda: f.read(4096), b""):
            h.update(chunk)
    return h.hexdigest()


# --------------------------------------------------------
# OCR & Extraction
# --------------------------------------------------------


def azure_ocr(image_bytes: bytes) -> str:
    analyze_url = AZURE_ENDPOINT.rstrip("/") + \
        "/formrecognizer/documentModels/prebuilt-read:analyze?api-version=2023-07-31-preview"
    headers = {
        "Ocp-Apim-Subscription-Key": AZURE_KEY,
        "Content-Type": "application/octet-stream"
    }
    resp = requests.post(analyze_url, headers=headers, data=image_bytes)
    resp.raise_for_status()
    op_url = resp.headers["operation-location"]
    for _ in range(15):
        result = requests.get(op_url, headers={"Ocp-Apim-Subscription-Key": AZURE_KEY}).json()
        if result.get("status") == "succeeded":
            lines = []
            for page in result["analyzeResult"]["pages"]:
                for line in page["lines"]:
                    lines.append(line["content"])
            return "\n".join(lines)
        time.sleep(2)
    return ""


def tesseract_ocr(image_bytes: bytes) -> str:
    img = Image.open(io.BytesIO(image_bytes))
    return pytesseract.image_to_string(img)


def extract_text_from_image(image_bytes: bytes) -> str:
    text = ""
    try:
        text = azure_ocr(image_bytes)
    except Exception as e:
        logger.warning(f"Azure OCR failed: {e}")
    if not text.strip():
        try:
            text = tesseract_ocr(image_bytes)
        except Exception as e:
            logger.warning(f"Tesseract OCR failed: {e}")
    return text


def extract_page_images(pdf_path: str) -> List[bytes]:
    doc = fitz.open(pdf_path)
    imgs = []
    for page in doc:
        pix = page.get_pixmap(dpi=300)
        imgs.append(pix.tobytes("png"))
    doc.close()
    return imgs


def extract_text_from_pdf(pdf_path: str) -> Tuple[str, List[str]]:
    warnings = []
    texts = []
    try:
        reader = PdfReader(pdf_path)
        for p in reader.pages:
            texts.append(p.extract_text() or "")
    except Exception as e:
        logger.warning(f"Digital extract failed: {e}")
        texts = []


    full = "\n".join(texts).strip()
    if len(full) < 50:
        texts = []
        for idx, img in enumerate(extract_page_images(pdf_path), start=1):
            t = extract_text_from_image(img)
            if not t.strip():
                warnings.append(f"Page {idx}: no text")
            texts.append(t)


    return "\n\n".join(texts), warnings

def build_db(rebuild: bool = Fals...

    st.set_page_config(page_title="Respiratory AI Assistant", layout="wide")

    with st.sidebar:
        st.header("📊 Database Management")

        def progress_update(fname, percent_done, remaining_sec):
            eta_str = f"{int(remaining_sec // 60)}m {int(remaining_sec % 60)}s" if remaining_sec > 60 else f"{int(remaining_sec)}s"
            status_placeholder.text(f"Processing: {fname} | {percent_done:.1f}% | ETA: {eta_str}")
            progress_bar.progress(int(percent_done))


        if st.button("🔄 Rebuild Database"):
            warnings = build_db(rebuild=True, progress_callback=progress_update)
            progress_bar.empty()

            if warnings:
                with st.expander("⚠️ Build Warnings"):
                    for w in warnings:
                        st.warning(w)

            warnings = build_db(rebuild=False, progress_callback=progress_update)
            progress_bar.empty()
            status_placeholder.success("Database updated successfully!")
            if warnings:
                with st.expander("⚠️ Update Warnings"):
                    for w in warnings:
                        st.warning(w)

        st.markdown("• Place PDF files in the `pdfs` folder\n• Rebuild DB when adding new documents\n• Update DB for incremental changes")


    # Ensure database exists
    if not os.path.exists(DB_DIR) or not os.listdir(DB_DIR):
        st.error("Database missing! Please add PDFs and build the database in the sidebar.")
        return


    # Question input centered
    st.markdown('<div style="background:#f8f9fa;padding:2rem;border-radius:10px;">', unsafe_allow_html=True)
    col1, col2, col3 = st.columns([1, 3, 1])
    with col2:
        st.markdown("### 🤔 Ask Your Respiratory Question")
        query = st.text_area("", placeholder="Enter your clinical question here...", height=100)
        st.markdown("*Append “\nAnswer without revealing your internal reasoning.” at the end of the prompt to prevent the model from inventing unsupported details.*")
        search = st.button("🔍 Get Answer")
    st.markdown("</div>", unsafe_allow_html=True)

        embeddings = HuggingFaceEmbeddings(model_name=EMBED_MODEL)
        store = Chroma(persist_directory=DB_DIR, embedding_function=embeddings)
        retriever = store.as_retriever(search_type="mmr", search_kwargs={"k": 20,  "fetch_k": 50, "lambda_mult": 0.5})

        # DEBUG: inspect retrieved docs
        for i, d in enumerate(docs, 1):
            logger.info(f"Doc {i} source={d.metadata.get('source')} "
                        f"preview={d.page_content[:400].replace('\n', ' ')}")

            template=(
                "You are an expert pulmonologist AI.\n"
                "Task: Provide a concise, evidence-based answer to the question using ONLY the provided context.\n"
                "Requirements:\n"

                "- Do not introduce information not covered in the context.\n"
                "- If context lacks an answer, state: \"Insufficient data in provided materials.\"\n\n"
                "Context:\n{context}\n\n"
                "Question:\n{question}\n\n"
                "Answer:\nAnswer without revealing your internal reasoning."
            ),
            input_variables=["context", "question"]
        ).format(context=context, question=query)


        llm = Ollama(model=OLLAMA_MODEL, temperature=0.0, max_tokens=512)
        answer = llm.invoke(prompt)


        if "[" not in answer:
            st.warning("⚠️ Check sources—some statements may be unsourced.")

is this OK?

### Answer
Mostly yes, but there are three important fixes to make it consistent with your new setup and avoid the meta‑tensor error and overly long prompts.



You already did this inside build_db, but not in main().

Change:
embeddings = HuggingFaceEmbeddings(model_name=EMBED_MODEL)
test_vec = embeddings.embed_query("test")

to:
embeddings = HuggingFaceEmbeddings(
    model_name=EMBED_MODEL,
    model_kwargs={"device": "cpu"}
)
test_vec = embeddings.embed_query("test")



Change:
if query and search:
    embeddings = HuggingFaceEmbeddings(model_name=EMBED_MODEL)
    store = Chroma(persist_directory=DB_DIR, embedding_function=embeddings)

to:
if query and search:
    embeddings = HuggingFaceEmbeddings(
        model_name=EMBED_MODEL,
        model_kwargs={"device": "cpu"}
    )
    store = Chroma(persist_directory=DB_DIR, embedding_function=embeddings)

This keeps SentenceTransformers on CPU and avoids the meta tensor device error you saw.



Right now you still have:
docs = retriever.invoke(query)
context = "\n\n".join(d.page_content for d in docs)

Replace that context line with the bounded version:
docs = retriever.invoke(query)
for i, d in enumerate(docs, 1):
    logger.info(
        f"Doc {i} source={d.metadata.get('source')} "
        f"preview={d.page_content[:400].replace('\n', ' ')}"
    )
max_chars = 15000
context = ""
for d in docs:
    if len(context) + len(d.page_content) > max_chars:
        break
    context += "\n\n" + d.page_content

Everything else below (PromptTemplate, llm.invoke, etc.) can stay as is.



If you want more structured, richer answers, you can replace the prompt block with the “stronger” version I suggested earlier:
prompt = PromptTemplate(
    template=(
        "You are an expert pulmonologist AI assistant.\n"
        "Use ONLY the information in the provided context to answer.\n\n"
        "Instructions:\n"
        "1. Start with a 1–3 sentence direct answer.\n"
        "2. Then, if the context allows, add brief bullet points for:\n"
        "   - Key recommendations\n"
        "   - Important thresholds / cutoffs\n"
        "   - When to admit, escalate, or refer\n"
        "3. Cite each important statement with its source file name "
        "(e.g. \"[source.pdf, pX]\").\n"
        "4. If the context does NOT clearly answer, say exactly: "
        "\"Insufficient data in provided materials.\" and nothing more.\n"
        "5. Do NOT use any information outside the context.\n\n"
        "Context:\n{context}\n\n"
        "Question:\n{question}\n\n"
        "Answer:\nAnswer without revealing your internal reasoning."
    ),
    input_variables=["context", "question"]
).format(context=context, question=query)



After these small edits:
HuggingFaceEmbeddings always uses device="cpu" → avoids torch meta‑tensor crash.  
Context is capped at ~15k characters → more stable, focused answers.  
Retrieval settings (mmr, k=20) and DB building on CPU are consistent.

So: yes, your file is almost there—apply steps 1 and 2 (and 3 if you want more informative answers), then restart Streamlit and test.

### Answer

def main():
    ensure_dir(PDF_DIR)
    ensure_dir(DB_DIR)

    # ✅ Test embedding model dimension (runs once at startup)
    embeddings = HuggingFaceEmbeddings(
        model_name=EMBED_MODEL,
        model_kwargs={"device": "cpu"}
    )
    test_vec = embeddings.embed_query("test")
    logger.info(f"✅ Embedding model: {EMBED_MODEL}, dimension: {len(test_vec)}")

    st.set_page_config(page_title="Respiratory AI Assistant", layout="wide")

    st.markdown(
        '<h1 style="text-align:center;color:#2E86AB;">🩺 Respiratory AI Assistant</h1>',
        unsafe_allow_html=True,
    )

    with st.sidebar:
        st.header("📊 Database Management")

        status_placeholder = st.empty()
        progress_bar = st.progress(0)

        def progress_update(fname, percent_done, remaining_sec):
            eta_str = (
                f"{int(remaining_sec // 60)}m {int(remaining_sec % 60)}s"
                if remaining_sec > 60
                else f"{int(remaining_sec)}s"
            )
            status_placeholder.text(
                f"Processing: {fname}  {percent_done:.1f}%  ETA: {eta_str}"
            )
            progress_bar.progress(int(percent_done))

        if st.button("🔄 Rebuild Database"):
            warnings = build_db(rebuild=True, progress_callback=progress_update)
            progress_bar.empty()
            status_placeholder.success("Database rebuilt successfully!")
            if warnings:
                with st.expander("⚠️ Build Warnings"):
                    for w in warnings:
                        st.warning(w)

        if st.button("📝 Update Database"):
            warnings = build_db(rebuild=False, progress_callback=progress_update)
            progress_bar.empty()
            status_placeholder.success("Database updated successfully!")
            if warnings:
                with st.expander("⚠️ Update Warnings"):
                    for w in warnings:
                        st.warning(w)

        st.markdown("")
        st.markdown(
            "• Place PDF files in the pdfs folder\n"
            "• Rebuild DB when adding new documents\n"
            "• Update DB for incremental changes"
        )

    # Ensure database exists
    if not os.path.exists(DB_DIR) or not os.listdir(DB_DIR):
        st.error("Database missing! Please add PDFs and build the database in the sidebar.")
        return

    # Question input centered
    st.markdown(
        '<div style="background:#f8f9fa;padding:2rem;border-radius:10px;">',
        unsafe_allow_html=True,
    )
    col1, col2, col3 = st.columns([1, 3, 1])
    with col2:
        st.markdown("### 🤔 Ask Your Respiratory Question")
        query = st.text_area(
            "",
            placeholder="Enter your clinical question here...",
            height=100,
        )
        st.markdown(
            "*Append “\nAnswer without revealing your internal reasoning.” at the end "
            "of the prompt to prevent the model from inventing unsupported details.*"
        )
        search = st.button("🔍 Get Answer")
    st.markdown("</div>", unsafe_allow_html=True)

    if query and search:
        embeddings = HuggingFaceEmbeddings(
            model_name=EMBED_MODEL,
            model_kwargs={"device": "cpu"},
        )
        store = Chroma(persist_directory=DB_DIR, embedding_function=embeddings)

        retriever = store.as_retriever(
            search_type="mmr",
            search_kwargs={"k": 20, "fetch_k": 50, "lambda_mult": 0.5},
        )
        docs = retriever.invoke(query)

        # DEBUG: inspect retrieved docs
        for i, d in enumerate(docs, 1):
            logger.info(
                f"Doc {i} source={d.metadata.get('source')} "
                f"preview={d.page_content[:400].replace('\n', ' ')}"
            )

        # Limit total context length so prompt doesn't explode
        max_chars = 15000
        context = ""
        for d in docs:
            if len(context) + len(d.page_content) > max_chars:
                break
            context += "\n\n" + d.page_content

        prompt = PromptTemplate(
            template=(
                "You are an expert pulmonologist AI.\n"
                "Task: Provide a concise, evidence-based answer to the question using "
                "ONLY the provided context.\n"
                "Requirements:\n"
                "- Cite each fact by chunk source (e.g., \"[source.pdf, page X]\").\n"
                "- Do not introduce information not covered in the context.\n"
                "- If context lacks an answer, state: \"Insufficient data in provided materials.\"\n\n"
                "Context:\n{context}\n\n"
                "Question:\n{question}\n\n"
                "Answer:\nAnswer without revealing your internal reasoning."
            ),
            input_variables=["context", "question"],
        ).format(context=context, question=query)

        llm = Ollama(model=OLLAMA_MODEL, temperature=0.0, max_tokens=512)
        answer = llm.invoke(prompt)

        if "[" not in answer:
            st.warning("⚠️ Check sources—some statements may be unsourced.")

        st.markdown(
            '<div style="background:#fff;padding:1.5rem;border-left:4px solid #2E86AB;'
            'border-radius:8px;">',
            unsafe_allow_html=True,
        )
        st.markdown("### 💡 Answer")
        st.markdown(answer)
        st.markdown("</div>", unsafe_allow_html=True)

        st.markdown(
            '<div style="background:#f1f3f4;padding:1rem;border-radius:5px;">',
            unsafe_allow_html=True,
        )
        st.markdown("### 📚 Sources")
        for d in docs:
            st.markdown(f"- {d.metadata['source']}")
        st.markdown("</div>", unsafe_allow_html=True)

    calculator_section()


if name == "main":
    main()

def ensure_dir(path: str):
    os.makedirs(path, exist_ok=True)


def file_hash(path: str) -> str:
    h = hashlib.md5()
    with open(path, "rb") as f:
        for chunk in iter(lambda: f.read(4096), b""):
            h.update(chunk)
    return h.hexdigest()


# --------------------------------------------------------
# OCR & Extraction
# --------------------------------------------------------


def azure_ocr(image_bytes: bytes) -> str:
    analyze_url = AZURE_ENDPOINT.rstrip("/") + \
        "/formrecognizer/documentModels/prebuilt-read:analyze?api-version=2023-07-31-preview"
    headers = {
        "Ocp-Apim-Subscription-Key": AZURE_KEY,
        "Content-Type": "application/octet-stream"
    }
    resp = requests.post(analyze_url, headers=headers, data=image_bytes)
    resp.raise_for_status()
    op_url = resp.headers["operation-location"]
    for _ in range(15):
        result = requests.get(op_url, headers={"Ocp-Apim-Subscription-Key": AZURE_KEY}).json()
        if result.get("status") == "succeeded":
            lines = []
            for page in result["analyzeResult"]["pages"]:
                for line in page["lines"]:
                    lines.append(line["content"])
            return "\n".join(lines)
        time.sleep(2)
    return ""


def tesseract_ocr(image_bytes: bytes) -> str:
    img = Image.open(io.BytesIO(image_bytes))
    return pytesseract.image_to_string(img)


def extract_text_from_image(image_bytes: bytes) -> str:
    text = ""
    try:
        text = azure_ocr(image_bytes)
    except Exception as e:
        logger.warning(f"Azure OCR failed: {e}")
    if not text.strip():
        try:
            text = tesseract_ocr(image_bytes)
        except Exception as e:
            logger.warning(f"Tesseract OCR failed: {e}")
    return text


def extract_page_images(pdf_path: str) -> List[bytes]:
    doc = fitz.open(pdf_path)
    imgs = []
    for page in doc:
        pix = page.get_pixmap(dpi=300)
        imgs.append(pix.tobytes("png"))
    doc.close()
    return imgs


def extract_text_from_pdf(pdf_path: str) -> Tuple[str, List[str]]:
    warnings = []
    texts = []
    try:
        reader = PdfReader(pdf_path)
        for p in reader.pages:
            texts.append(p.extract_text() or "")
    except Exception as e:
        logger.warning(f"Digital extract failed: {e}")
        texts = []


    full = "\n".join(texts).strip()
    if len(full) < 50:
        texts = []
        for idx, img in enumerate(extract_page_images(pdf_path), start=1):
            t = extract_text_from_image(img)

### Answer
To get richer, more “clinical approach” answers (history, exam, labs, imaging, treatment with drugs and doses), you mainly need to change the prompt and allow a bit more space in the output. Your retrieval and DB are already strong.

Here is a drop‑in replacement for the if query and search: block that makes the model systematically cover:
Clinical presentation (history, exam)  
Investigations (labs, imaging, other tests)  
Differential diagnosis  
Management plan with medications, doses, duration, and monitoring  
Follow‑up and red‑flags  

Replace your existing if query and search: block with this one (only this part changes; rest of file stays the same):
    if query and search:
        embeddings = HuggingFaceEmbeddings(
            model_name=EMBED_MODEL,
            model_kwargs={"device": "cpu"},
        )
        store = Chroma(persist_directory=DB_DIR, embedding_function=embeddings)

        retriever = store.as_retriever(
            search_type="mmr",
            search_kwargs={"k": 25, "fetch_k": 60, "lambda_mult": 0.4},
        )
        docs = retriever.invoke(query)

        # DEBUG: inspect retrieved docs
        for i, d in enumerate(docs, 1):
            logger.info(
                f"Doc {i} source={d.metadata.get('source')} "
                f"preview={d.page_content[:400].replace('\n', ' ')}"
            )

        # Limit total context length so prompt doesn't explode
        max_chars = 18000
        context = ""
        for d in docs:
            if len(context) + len(d.page_content) > max_chars:
                break
            context += "\n\n" + d.page_content

        prompt = PromptTemplate(
            template=(
                "You are an expert academic pulmonologist and intensivist.\n"
                "Use ONLY the information contained in the context to answer.\n\n"
                "For the disease or problem in the question, if the context allows, "
                "structure the answer into the following sections:\n"
                "1. Clinical presentation: typical history, risk factors, and key "
                "physical examination findings.\n"
                "2. Investigations:\n"
                "   - Laboratory tests (including important thresholds/cut-offs).\n"
                "   - Radiology and imaging (CXR, CT, ultrasound, etc.).\n"
                "   - Other tests (PFTs, bronchoscopy, echocardiography, etc.).\n"
                "3. Diagnosis and differential diagnosis: how to confirm the diagnosis "
                "and distinguish from common alternatives.\n"
                "4. Management and treatment:\n"
                "   - Initial stabilization (airway, breathing, circulation, oxygen, "
                "ventilation, fluids).\n"
                "   - Pharmacologic therapy with specific drug names, typical dose "
                "ranges, route, and duration when available in the context.\n"
                "   - Non‑pharmacologic measures (procedures, rehab, lifestyle, "
                "patient education).\n"
                "   - When to admit, ICU indications, and when to refer to a specialist.\n"
                "5. Follow‑up and monitoring: response assessment, treatment adjustment, "
                "and important red‑flags or complications.\n\n"
                "Rules:\n"
                "- Every important factual statement must be supported by the context.\n"
                "- Cite each major statement with its source file name (e.g. "
                "\"[source.pdf, pX]\").\n"
                "- If the context does NOT contain enough detail for a section, either "
                "omit that section or explicitly state that the data are insufficient.\n"
                "- NEVER invent drug names, doses, or recommendations that are not in "
                "the context. If the context is silent, say so.\n"
                "- If the context overall does not answer the question, reply exactly "
                "with: \"Insufficient data in provided materials.\" and nothing more.\n\n"
                "Context:\n{context}\n\n"
                "Question:\n{question}\n\n"
                "Answer:\nAnswer without revealing your internal reasoning."
            ),
            input_variables=["context", "question"],
        ).format(context=context, question=query)

        llm = Ollama(model=OLLAMA_MODEL, temperature=0.0, max_tokens=900)
        answer = llm.invoke(prompt)

        if "[" not in answer:
            st.warning("⚠️ Check sources—some statements may be unsourced.")

        st.markdown(
            '<div style="background:#fff;padding:1.5rem;border-left:4px solid #2E86AB;'
            'border-radius:8px;">',
            unsafe_allow_html=True,
        )
        st.markdown("### 💡 Answer")
        st.markdown(answer)
        st.markdown("</div>", unsafe_allow_html=True)

        st.markdown(
            '<div style="background:#f1f3f4;padding:1rem;border-radius:5px;">',
            unsafe_allow_html=True,
        )
        st.markdown("### 📚 Sources")
        for d in docs:
            st.markdown(f"- {d.metadata['source']}")
        st.markdown("</div>", unsafe_allow_html=True)

Key changes:
k raised to 25 and fetch_k to 60 → more chunks considered, better coverage.  
max_chars raised to 18,000 → more guideline text available in context.  
Prompt now forces a multi‑section clinical answer (presentation, investigations, differential, management with drugs, follow‑up).  
max_tokens increased to 900 to allow a detailed response.  

This will not magically create medications if they are not in your PDFs, but if your guidelines (BTS, ERS, GINA, WHO TB, etc.) include specific drugs and doses, the answers should now surface and organize them.

After you paste this block in, restart Streamlit and test with a question like:
“Approach to community‑acquired pneumonia in adults, including history, examination, investigations, and treatment.”  
“Management of malignant pleural effusion including procedures and pharmacologic therapy.”

## Turn 43
### Query
now make it able to follow the answers about the previous case and be able to continue disscusion not just give separate answers at a time

### Answer
Right now every question is answered in isolation. To “continue the discussion”, you need to:

1. Keep a short chat history in Streamlit state.  
2. Include that history in the LLM prompt so it sees the previous case and its own earlier answers.

Below is a minimal change that adds conversation awareness without rewriting your app.



Right after:
def main():
    ensure_dir(PDF_DIR)
    ensure_dir(DB_DIR)

add:
    # Initialize chat history in session state
    if "chat_history" not in st.session_state:
        st.session_state.chat_history = []  # list of {"role": "user"/"assistant", "content": str}



Replace your current if query and search: block with this version (it includes the “rich clinical” prompt we just designed, plus chat memory):
    if query and search:
        # 1) Update chat history with the new user message
        st.session_state.chat_history.append({"role": "user", "content": query})

        # 2) Build a compact conversation summary for the model
        #    (last 6 turns to keep context focused)
        recent_turns = st.session_state.chat_history[-6:]
        chat_context_text = ""
        for turn in recent_turns:
            role = "User" if turn["role"] == "user" else "Assistant"
            chat_context_text += f"{role}: {turn['content']}\n"

        # 3) Normal retrieval from your RAG database
        embeddings = HuggingFaceEmbeddings(
            model_name=EMBED_MODEL,
            model_kwargs={"device": "cpu"},
        )
        store = Chroma(persist_directory=DB_DIR, embedding_function=embeddings)

        retriever = store.as_retriever(
            search_type="mmr",
            search_kwargs={"k": 25, "fetch_k": 60, "lambda_mult": 0.4},
        )
        docs = retriever.invoke(query)

        # DEBUG: inspect retrieved docs
        for i, d in enumerate(docs, 1):
            logger.info(
                f"Doc {i} source={d.metadata.get('source')} "
                f"preview={d.page_content[:400].replace('\n', ' ')}"
            )

        # Limit total context length so prompt doesn't explode
        max_chars = 18000
        kb_context = ""
        for d in docs:
            if len(kb_context) + len(d.page_content) > max_chars:
                break
            kb_context += "\n\n" + d.page_content

        # 4) Build prompt that sees BOTH: previous conversation + KB context
        prompt = PromptTemplate(
            template=(
                "You are an expert academic pulmonologist and intensivist.\n"
                "You are chatting with a clinician about a specific case.\n"
                "Use ONLY the information contained in the context AND prior turns of "
                "this chat. If an item is not supported by either, do not invent it.\n\n"
                "Conversation so far:\n{chat_history}\n\n"
                "Retrieved knowledge base context (guidelines, reviews, etc.):\n"
                "{kb_context}\n\n"
                "For the latest user question, if the information is available, "
                "structure the answer into:\n"
                "1. Clinical presentation.\n"
                "2. Investigations (labs, imaging, other tests).\n"
                "3. Diagnosis and differential.\n"
                "4. Management and treatment (including specific medications, "
                "dose ranges, route, and duration when stated in the context).\n"
                "5. Follow‑up, monitoring, and red‑flags.\n\n"
                "Rules:\n"
                "- Respect the ongoing case: if the user asks a follow‑up question "
                "about 'this patient' or 'the previous CT', infer from the chat "
                "history what they refer to.\n"
                "- Every important factual statement must be supported by the "
                "knowledge base context.\n"
                "- Cite each major statement with its source file name "
                "(e.g. \"[source.pdf, pX]\").\n"
                "- If the context does NOT contain enough detail for a point, say so "
                "explicitly rather than guessing.\n"
                "- If the knowledge base overall does not answer the question, reply "
                "exactly: \"Insufficient data in provided materials.\" and nothing more.\n\n"
                "Latest user question:\n{question}\n\n"
                "Answer:\nAnswer without revealing your internal reasoning."
            ),
            input_variables=["chat_history", "kb_context", "question"],
        ).format(
            chat_history=chat_context_text,
            kb_context=kb_context,
            question=query,
        )

        llm = Ollama(model=OLLAMA_MODEL, temperature=0.0, max_tokens=900)
        answer = llm.invoke(prompt)

        # 5) Save assistant answer into chat history
        st.session_state.chat_history.append({"role": "assistant", "content": answer})

        if "[" not in answer:
            st.warning("⚠️ Check sources—some statements may be unsourced.")

        st.markdown(
            '<div style="background:#fff;padding:1.5rem;border-left:4px solid #2E86AB;'
            'border-radius:8px;">',
            unsafe_allow_html=True,
        )
        st.markdown("### 💡 Answer")
        st.markdown(answer)
        st.markdown("</div>", unsafe_allow_html=True)

        st.markdown(
            '<div style="background:#f1f3f4;padding:1rem;border-radius:5px;">',
            unsafe_allow_html=True,
        )
        st.markdown("### 📚 Sources")
        for d in docs:
            st.markdown(f"- {d.metadata['source']}")
        st.markdown("</div>", unsafe_allow_html=True)

What this gives you:
The assistant remembers previous turns within this browser session.  
Follow‑up questions like “How would you modify treatment if the patient has CKD stage 4?” or “What imaging should I order next in this case?” will be answered in the context of the previous case description and earlier answers, as long as those details were mentioned either by you or the model and supported by the KB.

If you want to also display the full chat history in the UI (like a chat log), you can add above the question box:
    # Show recent conversation
    if st.session_state.chat_history:
        st.markdown("### 🧵 Conversation so far")
        for turn in st.session_state.chat_history[-8:]:
            role = "You" if turn["role"] == "user" else "Assistant"
            st.markdown(f"{role}: {turn['content']}")

Place that just before the “Question input centered” block.

After these changes, restart Streamlit; ask a case description first, then follow with sequential questions—the model should now treat it as one continuous discussion instead of isolated queries.

## Turn 44

    # Show recent conversation
    if st.session_state.chat_history:

### Answer
Put it inside main(), after you check the database exists and before the “Ask Your Respiratory Question” UI block.

In your current main() you have this order:
    # Ensure database exists
    if not os.path.exists(DB_DIR) or not os.listdir(DB_DIR):
        st.error("Database missing! Please add PDFs and build the database in the sidebar.")
        return

    # Question input centered
    st.markdown(
        '<div style="background:#f8f9fa;padding:2rem;border-radius:10px;">',
        unsafe_allow_html=True,
    )
    col1, col2, col3 = st.columns([1, 3, 1])
    with col2:
        st.markdown("### 🤔 Ask Your Respiratory Question")

    # Ensure database exists

## Turn 45
### Query
it is super slow in answering!

### Answer
The slowness comes from three heavy steps happening on CPU every time you ask a question:

1. Loading BAAI/bge-large-en embeddings.  
2. Running the retriever on a big Chroma DB.  
3. Running llama3.2 in Ollama to generate a long, detailed answer.

You can make it much faster with a few surgical changes.



Right now you create HuggingFaceEmbeddings twice in main() (startup test + inside if query and search:). That reloads the model.

At the top of the file, after config, add a global cached embeddings object:
_EMBEDDINGS = None

def get_embeddings():
    global _EMBEDDINGS
    if _EMBEDDINGS is None:
        _EMBEDDINGS = HuggingFaceEmbeddings(
            model_name=EMBED_MODEL,
            model_kwargs={"device": "cpu"},
        )
    return _EMBEDDINGS

Then in main():
Remove the startup test (or keep it but use get_embeddings()):
    # ✅ Test embedding model dimension (runs once at startup)
    embeddings = get_embeddings()
    test_vec = embeddings.embed_query("test")
    logger.info(f"✅ Embedding model: {EMBED_MODEL}, dimension: {len(test_vec)}")
And in the QA block, replace:
        embeddings = HuggingFaceEmbeddings(
            model_name=EMBED_MODEL,
            model_kwargs={"device": "cpu"},
        )

with:
        embeddings = get_embeddings()

Also in build_db, replace creation with get_embeddings():
    embeddings = get_embeddings()

This avoids re‑initializing the model on every question and DB build.



We made the model very “thorough” by:
k=25, fetch_k=60  
max_chars = 18000  

To speed up, tune them down a bit:

In the QA block, change:
        retriever = store.as_retriever(
            search_type="mmr",
            search_kwargs={"k": 25, "fetch_k": 60, "lambda_mult": 0.4},
        )

to:
        retriever = store.as_retriever(
            search_type="mmr",
            search_kwargs={"k": 12, "fetch_k": 30, "lambda_mult": 0.5},
        )

And:
        max_chars = 18000

to:
        max_chars = 9000

This cuts roughly in half:
Number of chunks to embed and send to LLM.  
Prompt size → faster generation.

You still get multi‑source answers but with less overhead.



You increased max_tokens to 900, which is great for depth but slow. You can compromise:
        llm = Ollama(model=OLLAMA_MODEL, temperature=0.0, max_tokens=600)

600 still allows a structured, rich answer but reduces generation time.



If you click Rebuild / Update Database while also asking questions, both operations share CPU and disk.

When you’re in “chat mode”:
Don’t click DB buttons.  
Or you can disable them while a question is running, but simplest is: rebuild first, then chat.



In OLLAMA_MODEL = "llama3.2:latest":
If llama3.2 in your setup is 70B or heavily quantized, it will be slow on CPU.  
For speed, you can switch to a lighter model (only if you have it installed), e.g.:
OLLAMA_MODEL = "llama3.2:8b"

or another small, good medical‑capable model you have locally.



1. Add global get_embeddings() once, use it everywhere.  
2. In QA block:
k 12, fetch_k 30, max_chars 9000.  
max_tokens 600.  
3. Avoid running DB builds while chatting.

After these changes, restart Streamlit and test again. If you want, paste your updated get_embeddings() and QA block and I can double‑check they’re wired correctly.

---

def ensure_dir(path: str):
    os.makedirs(path, exist_ok=True)


def file_hash(path: str) -> str:
    h = hashlib.md5()
    with open(path, "rb") as f:
        for chunk in iter(lambda: f.read(4096), b""):
            h.update(chunk)
    return h.hexdigest()


# --------------------------------------------------------
# OCR & Extraction
# --------------------------------------------------------


def azure_ocr(image_bytes: bytes) -> str:
    analyze_url = AZURE_ENDPOINT.rstrip("/") + \
        "/formrecognizer/documentModels/prebuilt-read:analyze?api-version=2023-07-31-preview"
    headers = {
        "Ocp-Apim-Subscription-Key": AZURE_KEY,
        "Content-Type": "application/octet-stream"
    }
    resp = requests.post(analyze_url, headers=headers, data=image_bytes)
    resp.raise_for_status()
    op_url = resp.headers["operation-location"]
    for _ in range(15):
        result = requests.get(op_url, headers={"Ocp-Apim-Subscription-Key": AZURE_KEY}).json()
        if result.get("status") == "succeeded":
            lines = []
            for page in result["analyzeResult"]["pages"]:
                for line in page["lines"]:
                    lines.append(line["content"])
            return "\n".join(lines)
        time.sleep(2)
    return ""


def tesseract_ocr(image_bytes: bytes) -> str:
    img = Image.open(io.BytesIO(image_bytes))
    return pytesseract.image_to_string(img)


def extract_text_from_image(image_bytes: bytes) -> str:
    text = ""
    try:
        text = azure_ocr(image_bytes)
    except Exception as e:
        logger.warning(f"Azure OCR failed: {e}")
    if not text.strip():
        try:
            text = tesseract_ocr(image_bytes)
        except Exception as e:
            logger.warning(f"Tesseract OCR failed: {e}")
    return text


def extract_page_images(pdf_path: str) -> List[bytes]:
    doc = fitz.open(pdf_path)
    imgs = []
    for page in doc:
        pix = page.get_pixmap(dpi=300)
        imgs.append(pix.tobytes("png"))
    doc.close()
    return imgs


def extract_text_from_pdf(pdf_path: str) -> Tuple[str, List[str]]:
    warnings = []
    texts = []
    try:
        reader = PdfReader(pdf_path)
        for p in reader.pages:
            texts.append(p.extract_text() or "")
    except Exception as e:
        logger.warning(f"Digital extract failed: {e}")
        texts = []


    full = "\n".join(texts).strip()
    if len(full) < 50:
        texts = []
        for idx, img in enumerate(extract_page_images(pdf_path), start=1):
            t = extract_text_from_image(img)
            if not t.strip():
                warnings.append(f"Page {idx}: no text")
            texts.append(t)


    return "\n\n".join(texts), warnings

### Answer
To change your corpus (delete some PDFs, add new ones) and keep everything consistent, do this:

1. Stop Streamlit.  
2. Go to:

   text
   D:\Dev\Active\RespAI_Project\pdfs
   

3. Delete the PDFs you no longer want indexed (move them out of this folder).  
4. Copy the new PDFs you want into this same pdfs folder.

At this moment, the Chroma DB still contains vectors from the old PDFs, and processed_files.json still remembers hashes for deleted files. So you need a clean rebuild.



Because your build_db(rebuild=True, ...) already handles resetting the DB, the easiest path is:

1. Start your venv and Streamlit:

   powershell
   cd D:\Dev\Active\RespAI_Project
   .\venv\Scripts\Activate.ps1
   streamlit run main_resp_ai_The_Final_Version.py
   

2. In the sidebar, click “🔄 Rebuild Database”.

What this does in your code:
rebuild=True triggers:

  python
  if rebuild:
      shutil.rmtree(DB_DIR)
      ensure_dir(DB_DIR)
      processed = {}
  

  So:
Entire chroma_db folder is deleted and recreated.  
processed_files.json is reset to {}.
Then it reads only the current contents of pdfs/:

  python
  pdfs = [f for f in os.listdir(PDF_DIR) if f.lower().endswith(".pdf")]
  

  and rebuilds the database from exactly those PDFs.  

Result:  
Removed PDFs → no longer in DB.  
New PDFs → fully extracted, chunked, and embedded.

You don’t need to manually touch Chroma internals for deletion; the rebuild wipes everything and reindexes.



You can achieve the same as “Rebuild Database” by:
cd D:\Dev\Active\RespAI_Project
rmdir /s /q chroma_db
del processed_files.json
python build_new_db.py_V2.py

or by running the Streamlit app and pressing Rebuild as above.



Once the PDFs are in their final shape and the DB is rebuilt:
Apply the global get_embeddings() optimization and retrieval/prompt tweaks we discussed to speed up answers.  
Restart Streamlit and start using the new corpus.

This “delete/add PDFs → Rebuild DB” pattern is safe and keeps your Chroma index perfectly aligned with the pdfs folder content.

## Turn 47
### Query
I want to use this feature : In the sidebar, click “🔄 Rebuild Database”, so make it display what is going on on real time in the same sidebar with informative messages and a final message when done

### Answer
You already have the right wiring; we just need to polish the sidebar feedback so it’s clearer and shows a final “done” message.

Here is a drop‑in replacement for the sidebar part of main() that:
Shows a live progress bar and ETA while rebuilding/updating.  
Writes clear status messages (“Starting…”, “Processing: …”, “Completed”).  
Shows a final success box when done.

Replace everything inside with st.sidebar: in main() with this:
    with st.sidebar:
        st.header("📊 Database Management")

        status_placeholder = st.empty()          # For live status text
        progress_bar = st.progress(0)           # For numeric progress
        phase_placeholder = st.empty()          # For high-level phase message

        def progress_update(fname, percent_done, remaining_sec):
            # Called from build_db() for each file
            if remaining_sec > 60:
                eta_str = f"{int(remaining_sec // 60)}m {int(remaining_sec % 60)}s"
            else:
                eta_str = f"{int(remaining_sec)}s"

            phase_placeholder.info("🔧 Building / updating Chroma database...")
            status_placeholder.text(
                f"Processing: {fname}\n"
                f"Progress: {percent_done:.1f}%  ETA: {eta_str}"
            )
            progress_bar.progress(int(percent_done))

        # Rebuild button = full reset and reindex
        if st.button("🔄 Rebuild Database"):
            phase_placeholder.info("♻️ Full rebuild started...")
            status_placeholder.text("Scanning PDFs and extracting text...")
            progress_bar.progress(0)

            warnings = build_db(rebuild=True, progress_callback=progress_update)

            # Final messages
            progress_bar.progress(100)
            phase_placeholder.success("✅ Rebuild completed successfully.")
            status_placeholder.text("All documents re-indexed from the current pdfs folder.")

            if warnings:
                with st.expander("⚠️ Build Warnings"):
                    for w in warnings:
                        st.warning(w)

        # Incremental update button = add/refresh new/changed PDFs
        if st.button("📝 Update Database"):
            phase_placeholder.info("📥 Incremental update started...")
            status_placeholder.text("Checking for new or modified PDFs...")
            progress_bar.progress(0)

            warnings = build_db(rebuild=False, progress_callback=progress_update)

            progress_bar.progress(100)
            phase_placeholder.success("✅ Update completed successfully.")
            status_placeholder.text("New and changed documents have been indexed.")

            if warnings:
                with st.expander("⚠️ Update Warnings"):
                    for w in warnings:
                        st.warning(w)

        st.markdown("")
        st.markdown(
            "• Place PDF files in the pdfs folder\n"
            "• Use Rebuild after big changes (add/remove many PDFs)\n"
            "• Use Update for small incremental additions"
        )

How it behaves:
When you click Rebuild or Update, the sidebar shows:
A phase message (e.g., “Full rebuild started…”, then “Building / updating Chroma database…”).  
A live percentage and ETA line.  
Progress bar moving as build_db iterates through PDFs.  
At the end, the bar jumps to 100%, and you see a green success message and a stable status text.  

No changes are needed in build_db; it already calls progress_callback(fname, percent_done, remaining) in real time.

## Turn 48
### Query
why it is starting from scratch, is it better to read the new pdf folder and if a pdf is already found let it keep it and skip to the next this way it will be faster.
what do you think?

### Answer
Your intuition is right: for most day‑to‑day use, incremental update that skips unchanged PDFs is better and faster. Rebuild from scratch is only needed when you deliberately want a clean slate (for example after deleting many PDFs or changing the embedding model).

Given your current setup:
“📝 Update Database” already does what you described:
Reads all PDFs in pdfs/.  
For each file, compares its md5 hash with what’s stored in processed_files.json.  
If hash unchanged → skips extraction and re‑embedding.  
If new or modified → extracts, chunks, and calls store.add_documents(chunks), appending to the existing Chroma DB.
“🔄 Rebuild Database” intentionally starts from scratch:
Deletes chroma_db/.  
Resets processed_files.json.  
Re‑indexes everything from the current pdfs.  

So:
When you only add new PDFs, or you edit/replace a few PDFs → click Update Database (fast, incremental).  
When you remove PDFs and want them completely gone from the DB, or after big surgery on the corpus / model change → click Rebuild Database (slow, clean).

Because you want to delete some PDFs and add many others, doing a one‑time rebuild now is correct: it guarantees old documents are removed from the DB. After this, for future additions, stick to Update so it only processes new/changed hashes and skips the rest.

---

## Turn 49
### Query
what if i want to use

### Answer
Using build_new_db.py_V2.py is still useful in two main scenarios:
When you want a big, resumable offline build on D:\new_chroma_db_V2 with rich console logs.
When you want to recover from a crash or build on another machine, then copy the ready DB into your app.

You now have *two* ways to manage the DB:
Operate on: BASE_DIR/chroma_db (inside the project).
Rebuild Database:
Deletes chroma_db and processed_files.json.  
Re‑extracts and re‑indexes everything from current pdfs.  
Update Database:
Uses hashes to skip unchanged PDFs.  
Adds only new/changed ones.

Use this path for day‑to‑day work, especially after you add/remove PDFs in pdfs.
Operates on: D:\new_chroma_db_V2.
Tracks:
processed_files.json → text extracted per PDF.  
indexed_files.json → which PDFs already added to Chroma.  
Behavior:
Skips PDFs already extracted and indexed.  
Only processes missing/incomplete ones, very resilient to crashes.

If you “want to use it” now, the flow is:

1. Put your final PDF set into RespAI_Project\pdfs.  
2. Run:

   powershell
   cd D:\Dev\Active\RespAI_Project
   .\venv\Scripts\Activate.ps1
   python build_new_db.py_V2.py
   

3. When it finishes successfully, copy the built DB into your app:

   powershell
   xcopy /E /I "D:\new_chroma_db_V2" "D:\Dev\Active\RespAI_Project\chroma_db"
   

4. Restart Streamlit.

So:  
For one heavy, resumable build on D: → use build_new_db.py_V2.py.
For frequent incremental updates from inside the UI → use the sidebar Update/Rebuild buttons in main_resp_ai_The_Final_Version.py.

and delete the surrounding triple quotes, or

main_resp_ai_The_Final_Version.py — Respiratory AI Assistant with improved UI and build progress feedback

## Turn 53
### Query
what are these?

### Answer
Those are Streamlit’s file‑watcher controls indicating your app script changed.
“File change.”: Streamlit detected that main_resp_ai_The_Final_Version.py (or another imported file) was modified.
“Rerun”: Runs the script once more immediately with the new code.  
“Always rerun”: Automatically reruns the app every time it detects a file change (useful while actively editing).  

So when you edit/save your Python file, click Rerun once, or enable Always rerun while you’re iterating.

---

## Turn 54
### Query
let's change this to be more friendly with tracking and showing the chats one after the other use pleasant colors

### Answer
Those controls are part of Streamlit’s “live reload” UI that help you manage code changes while the app is running.
File change.  
  Streamlit detected that a source file (such as your app script) has changed. This indicates that the app is out of sync with the current code version. Clicking this will rerun your app from the beginning using the latest code.
Rerun  
  This button reruns your app immediately. It’s useful when you’ve made code edits and want to apply them without restarting the server manually.
Always rerun  
  When enabled, this automatically reruns your app every time it detects a file change. This keeps your app continuously up to date as you edit your script, which is convenient during active development sessions.

---

## Turn 56
### Query
i mean واجهة التطبيق

### Answer
تمام، فهمتك تقصد واجهة التطبيق نفسها (UI) وطريقة عرض المحادثة.  

خلينا نعمل خطوتين واضحين، وأعطيك كود جاهز تعدله في main_resp_ai_The_Final_Version.py:

في أعلى الملف بعد import streamlit as st أضف هذا:
st.set_page_config(
    page_title="Respiratory AI Assistant",
    page_icon="🫁",
    layout="centered",
    initial_sidebar_state="collapsed"
)
CUSTOM_CSS = """
<style>
body {
    background-color: #f5f7fb;
}
[data-testid="stAppViewContainer"] {
    background: linear-gradient(180deg, #f5f7fb 0%, #eef3ff 40%, #ffffff 100%);
}
[data-testid="stHeader"] {
    background: rgba(0,0,0,0);
}
.chat-bubble-user {
    background-color: #d1e8ff;
    color: #003366;
    padding: 12px 16px;
    border-radius: 18px 18px 0 18px;
    margin-bottom: 8px;
}
.chat-bubble-assistant {
    background-color: #ffffff;
    color: #202124;
    padding: 12px 16px;
    border-radius: 18px 18px 18px 0;
    margin-bottom: 8px;
    border: 1px solid #dde3f0;
}
.chat-meta {
    font-size: 0.75rem;
    color: #6b7280;
    margin-bottom: 4px;
}
.chat-container {
    padding: 1rem;
    background-color: #f0f4ff;
    border-radius: 16px;
    border: 1px solid #dde3f0;
}
</style>
st.markdown(CUSTOM_CSS, unsafe_allow_html=True)

هذا يعطيك خلفية فاتحة بدرجات أزرق/بنفسجي لطيف، مع فقاعات دردشة بألوان مختلفة للمستخدم والمساعد.

افترض أن عندك session state للمحادثة، لو ما عندك أضف هذا قريب من بداية main() أو قبل UI:
if "chat_history" not in st.session_state:
    st.session_state.chat_history = []  # list of dicts: {"role": "user"/"assistant", "content": "text"}

بعد ما ترسل السؤال للموديل وتحصل على الإجابة، أضفهما للتاريخ:
def add_to_history(user_message: str, assistant_reply: str):
    st.session_state.chat_history.append({"role": "user", "content": user_message})
    st.session_state.chat_history.append({"role": "assistant", "content": assistant_reply})

وفي المكان الذي فيه زر Get Answer (أو أي اسم) بعد حساب الإجابة مباشرة:
if st.button("🔍 Get Answer"):
    question = user_input.strip()
    if question:
        # هنا تستدعي موديلك وترجع الجواب في متغير مثلا: answer_text
        answer_text = run_model(question)  # عدّل حسب دالتك
        add_to_history(question, answer_text)

ثم تحت هذا الجزء اعرض المحادثة بشكل جميل:
st.markdown("### 🗂️ محادثاتك الأخيرة")
st.markdown('<div class="chat-container">', unsafe_allow_html=True)

for i, msg in enumerate(st.session_state.chat_history):
    role = "🧑⚕️ أنت" if msg["role"] == "user" else "🤖 المساعد"
    bubble_class = "chat-bubble-user" if msg["role"] == "user" else "chat-bubble-assistant"

    st.markdown(
        f"""
        <div class="chat-meta">{role}</div>
        <div class="{bubble_class}">{msg["content"]}</div>
        """,
        unsafe_allow_html=True,
    )

st.markdown("</div>", unsafe_allow_html=True)

لو أرسلت لي جزء الكود المسؤول عن استقبال السؤال والرد من الموديل (run_model أو المكافئ عندك)، أقدر أدمج لك كل هذا مباشرة في نفس البلوك بحيث تنسخ‑تلصق فقط.

where to find جزء الكود المسؤول عن استقبال السؤال والرد answer in english

import os
import json
import time
import logging
import hashlib
import shutil
import io


import streamlit as st
import fitz  # PyMuPDF
import pytesseract
import requests
from PIL import Image
from typing import List, Tuple


# --- قسم الاستيراد المحدث (2026 Standard) ---
from langchain_ollama import OllamaLLM as Ollama
from langchain_huggingface import HuggingFaceEmbeddings
from langchain_chroma import Chroma
from langchain_core.documents import Document  # التغيير هنا
from langchain_core.prompts import PromptTemplate # التغيير هنا
from langchain_text_splitters import RecursiveCharacterTextSplitter # التغيير هنا
from PyPDF2 import PdfReader

# --------------------------------------------------------
# Configuration
# --------------------------------------------------------

logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)


BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))
import pytesseract
# قم بتغيير المسار حسب مكان تثبيت البرنامج في C عندك
pytesseract.pytesseract.tesseract_cmd = r'C:\Program Files\Tesseract-OCR\tesseract.exe'
PDF_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "pdfs")
DB_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "chroma_db")

# تأكد من وجود المجلدات لكي لا ينهار البرنامج
os.makedirs(PDF_DIR, exist_ok=True)
os.makedirs(DB_DIR, exist_ok=True)


EMBED_MODEL = "BAAI/bge-large-en"
OLLAMA_MODEL = "llama3.2:latest"  # Use your preferred model


AZURE_ENDPOINT = "https://respai-rg.cognitiveservices.azure.com/"
AZURE_KEY = os.getenv("AZURE_KEY")


# pytesseract.pytesseract.tesseract_cmd = r"C:\Program Files\Tesseract-OCR\tesseract.exe"


# --------------------------------------------------------
# Helpers
# --------------------------------------------------------


def ensure_dir(path: str):
    os.makedirs(path, exist_ok=True)


def file_hash(path: str) -> str:
    h = hashlib.md5()
    with open(path, "rb") as f:
        for chunk in iter(lambda: f.read(4096), b""):
            h.update(chunk)
    return h.hexdigest()


# --------------------------------------------------------
# OCR & Extraction
# --------------------------------------------------------


def azure_ocr(image_bytes: bytes) -> str:
    analyze_url = AZURE_ENDPOINT.rstrip("/") + \
        "/formrecognizer/documentModels/prebuilt-read:analyze?api-version=2023-07-31-preview"
    headers = {
        "Ocp-Apim-Subscription-Key": AZURE_KEY,
        "Content-Type": "application/octet-stream"
    }
    resp = requests.post(analyze_url, headers=headers, data=image_bytes)
    resp.raise_for_status()
    op_url = resp.headers["operation-location"]
    for _ in range(15):
        result = requests.get(op_url, headers={"Ocp-Apim-Subscription-Key": AZURE_KEY}).json()
        if result.get("status") == "succeeded":
            lines = []
            for page in result["analyzeResult"]["pages"]:
                for line in page["lines"]:
                    lines.append(line["content"])
            return "\n".join(lines)
        time.sleep(2)
    return ""


def tesseract_ocr(image_bytes: bytes) -> str:
    img = Image.open(io.BytesIO(image_bytes))
    return pytesseract.image_to_string(img)


def extract_text_from_image(image_bytes: bytes) -> str:
    text = ""
    try:
        text = azure_ocr(image_bytes)
    except Exception as e:
        logger.warning(f"Azure OCR failed: {e}")
    if not text.strip():
        try:
            text = tesseract_ocr(image_bytes)
        except Exception as e:
            logger.warning(f"Tesseract OCR failed: {e}")
    return text


def extract_page_images(pdf_path: str) -> List[bytes]:
    doc = fitz.open(pdf_path)
    imgs = []
    for page in doc:
        pix = page.get_pixmap(dpi=300)
        imgs.append(pix.tobytes("png"))
    doc.close()
    return imgs


def extract_text_from_pdf(pdf_path: str) -> Tuple[str, List[str]]:
    warnings = []
    texts = []
    try:
        reader = PdfReader(pdf_path)
        for p in reader.pages:
            texts.append(p.extract_text() or "")
    except Exception as e:
        logger.warning(f"Digital extract failed: {e}")
        texts = []


    full = "\n".join(texts).strip()
    if len(full) < 50:
        texts = []
        for idx, img in enumerate(extract_page_images(pdf_path), start=1):
            t = extract_text_from_image(img)
            if not t.strip():
                warnings.append(f"Page {idx}: no text")
            texts.append(t)


    return "\n\n".join(texts), warnings


# --------------------------------------------------------
# Build/Update DB with progress feedback
# ----------------------...

...arch = st.button("🔍 Get Answer")
    st.markdown("</div>", unsafe_allow_html=True)


    if query and search:
        # 1) Update chat history with the new user message
        st.session_state.chat_history.append({"role": "user", "content": query})


        # 2) Build a compact conversation summary for the model
        #    (last 6 turns to keep context focused)
        recent_turns = st.session_state.chat_history[-6:]
        chat_context_text = ""
        for turn in recent_turns:
            role = "User" if turn["role"] == "user" else "Assistant"
            chat_context_text += f"{role}: {turn['content']}\n"


        # 3) Normal retrieval from your RAG database
        embeddings = HuggingFaceEmbeddings(
            model_name=EMBED_MODEL,
            model_kwargs={"device": "cpu"},
        )
        store = Chroma(persist_directory=DB_DIR, embedding_function=embeddings)


        retriever = store.as_retriever(
            search_type="mmr",
            search_kwargs={"k": 25, "fetch_k": 60, "lambda_mult": 0.4},
        )
        docs = retriever.invoke(query)


        # DEBUG: inspect retrieved docs
        for i, d in enumerate(docs, 1):
            logger.info(
                f"Doc {i} source={d.metadata.get('source')} "
                f"preview={d.page_content[:400].replace('\n', ' ')}"
            )


        # Limit total context length so prompt doesn't explode
        max_chars = 18000
        kb_context = ""
        for d in docs:
            if len(kb_context) + len(d.page_content) > max_chars:
                break
            kb_context += "\n\n" + d.page_content


        # 4) Build prompt that sees BOTH: previous conversation + KB context
        prompt = PromptTemplate(
            template=(
                "You are an expert academic pulmonologist and intensivist.\n"
                "You are chatting with a clinician about a specific case.\n"
                "Use ONLY the information contained in the context AND prior turns of "
                "this chat. If an item is not supported by either, do not invent it.\n\n"
                "Conversation so far:\n{chat_history}\n\n"
                "Retrieved knowledge base context (guidelines, reviews, etc.):\n"
                "{kb_context}\n\n"
                "For the latest user question, if the information is available, "
                "structure the answer into:\n"
                "1. Clinical presentation.\n"
                "2. Investigations (labs, imaging, other tests).\n"
                "3. Diagnosis and differential.\n"
                "4. Management and treatment (including specific medications, "
                "dose ranges, route, and duration when stated in the context).\n"
                "5. Follow‑up, monitoring, and red‑flags.\n\n"
                "Rules:\n"
                "- Respect the ongoing case: if the user asks a follow‑up question "
                "about 'this patient' or 'the previous CT', infer from the chat "
                "history what they refer to.\n"
                "- Every important factual statement must be supported by the "
                "knowledge base context.\n"
                "- Cite each major statement with its source file name "
                "(e.g. \"[source.pdf, pX]\").\n"
                "- If the context does NOT contain enough detail for a point, say so "
                "explicitly rather than guessing.\n"
                "- If the knowledge base overall does not answer the question, reply "
                "exactly: \"Insufficient data in provided materials.\" and nothing more.\n\n"
                "Latest user question:\n{question}\n\n"
                "Answer:\nAnswer without revealing your internal reasoning."
            ),
            input_variables=["chat_history", "kb_context", "question"],
        ).format(
            chat_history=chat_context_text,
            kb_context=kb_context,
            question=query,
        )


        llm = Ollama(model=OLLAMA_MODEL, temperature=0.0, max_tokens=900)
        answer = llm.invoke(prompt)


        # 5) Save assistant answer into chat history
        st.session_state.chat_history.append({"role": "assistant", "content": answer})


        if "[" not in answer:
            st.warning("⚠️ Check sources—some statements may be unsourced.")


        st.markdown(
            '<div style="background:#fff;padding:1.5rem;border-left:4px solid #2E86AB;'
            'border-radius:8px;">',
            unsafe_allow_html=True,
        )
        st.markdown("### 💡 Answer")
        st.markdown(answer)
        st.markdown("</div>", unsafe_allow_html=True)


        st.markdown(
            '<div style="background:#f1f3f4;padding:1rem;border-radius:5px;">',
            unsafe_allow_html=True,
        )
        st.markdown("### 📚 Sources")
        for d in docs:
            st.markdown(f"- {d.metadata['source']}")
        st.markdown("</div>", unsafe_allow_html=True)



    calculator_section()



if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

### Answer
In your current file, the “code that receives the question and returns the answer” is already clearly grouped in main() under the if query and search: block.
This part reads the user’s text and button click:  
query = st.text_area(
    "",
    placeholder="Enter your clinical question here...",
    height=100,
)
...
search = st.button("🔍 Get Answer")
...
if query and search:
Here query is the user question and search is the “Get Answer” button state.
Inside that same if query and search: block you already:  
Append the user message to st.session_state.chat_history.  
Build chat_context_text from recent turns.  
Run retrieval from Chroma using retriever.invoke(query).  
Build a PromptTemplate and format it with chat_history, kb_context, and question.  
Instantiate llm = Ollama(...) and call:  
answer = llm.invoke(prompt)
This line is exactly where the LLM processes the question plus context and generates the answer.
Immediately after that you:  
Append the assistant reply to chat history:
st.session_state.chat_history.append({"role": "assistant", "content": answer})
Render the answer block (### 💡 Answer) and the sources list.

So if you want to refactor for a nicer chat UI, you can extract everything inside if query and search: into a helper like def run_model(question: str) -> str: and call it from there, then use st.session_state.chat_history to display bubbles as we discussed.

---

                "- Cite each major statement with its source file name "
                "(e.g. \"[source.pdf, pX]\").\n"
                "- If the context does NOT contain enough detail for a point, say so "
                "explicitly rather than guessing.\n"
                "- If the knowledge base overall does not answer the question, reply "
                "exactly: \"Insufficient data in provided materials.\" and nothing more.\n\n"
                "Latest user question:\n{question}\n\n"
                "Answer:\nAnswer without revealing your internal reasoning."
            ),
            input_variables=["chat_history", "kb_context", "question"],
        ).format(
            chat_history=chat_context_text,
            kb_context=kb_context,
            question=query,
        )

Inside main() (top of the function), keep:
if "chat_history" not in st.session_state:
    st.session_state.chat_history = []  # list of {"role": "user"/"assistant", "content": str}


Now replace your existing if query and search: block with this:
if query and search:
    # 1) Add user message to history
    st.session_state.chat_history.append({"role": "user", "content": query})

    # 2) Build compact conversation summary (last 6 turns) for the model
    recent_turns = st.session_state.chat_history[-6:]
    chat_context_text = ""
    for turn in recent_turns:
        role = "User" if turn["role"] == "user" else "Assistant"
        chat_context_text += f"{role}: {turn['content']}\n"

    # 3) Retrieval from RAG database
    embeddings = HuggingFaceEmbeddings(
        model_name=EMBED_MODEL,
        model_kwargs={"device": "cpu"},
    )
    store = Chroma(persist_directory=DB_DIR, embedding_function=embeddings)

    retriever = store.as_retriever(
        search_type="mmr",
        search_kwargs={"k": 25, "fetch_k": 60, "lambda_mult": 0.4},
    )
    docs = retriever.invoke(query)

    # DEBUG: inspect retrieved docs
    for i, d in enumerate(docs, 1):
        logger.info(
            f"Doc {i} source={d.metadata.get('source')} "
            f"preview={d.page_content[:400].replace('\n', ' ')}"
        )

    # Limit total context length
    max_chars = 18000
    kb_context = ""
    for d in docs:
        if len(kb_context) + len(d.page_content) > max_chars:
            break
        kb_context += "\n\n" + d.page_content

    # 4) Build prompt with chat history + KB context
    prompt = PromptTemplate(
        template=(
            "You are an expert academic pulmonologist and intensivist.\n"
            "You are chatting with a clinician about a specific case.\n"
            "Use ONLY the information contained in the context AND prior turns of "
            "this chat. If an item is not supported by either, do not invent it.\n\n"
            "Conversation so far:\n{chat_history}\n\n"
            "Retrieved knowledge base context (guidelines, reviews, etc.):\n"
            "{kb_context}\n\n"
            "For the latest user question, if the information is available, "
            "structure the answer into:\n"
            "1. Clinical presentation.\n"
            "2. Investigations (labs, imaging, other tests).\n"
            "3. Diagnosis and differential.\n"
            "4. Management and treatment (including specific medications, "
            "dose ranges, route, and duration when stated in the context).\n"
            "5. Follow‑up, monitoring, and red‑flags.\n\n"
            "Rules:\n"
            "- Respect the ongoing case: if the user asks a follow‑up question "
            "about 'this patient' or 'the previous CT', infer from the chat "
            "history what they refer to.\n"
            "- Every important factual statement must be supported by the "
            "knowledge base context.\n"
            "- Cite each major statement with its source file name "
            "(e.g. \"[source.pdf, pX]\").\n"
            "- If the context does NOT contain enough detail for a point, say so "
            "explicitly rather than guessing.\n"
            "- If the knowledge base overall does not answer the question, reply "
            "exactly: \"Insufficient data in provided materials.\" and nothing more.\n\n"
            "Latest user question:\n{question}\n\n"
            "Answer:\nAnswer without revealing your internal reasoning."
        ),
        input_variables=["chat_history", "kb_context", "question"],
    ).format(
        chat_history=chat_context_text,
        kb_context=kb_context,
        question=query,
    )

    llm = Ollama(model=OLLAMA_MODEL, temperature=0.0, max_tokens=900)
    answer = llm.invoke(prompt)

    # 5) Save assistant answer into chat history
    st.session_state.chat_history.append({"role": "assistant", "content": answer})

    if "[" not in answer:
        st.warning("⚠️ Check sources—some statements may be unsourced.")

    # 6) Nice chat-style rendering (user + assistant bubbles)
    st.markdown("### 🗂️ Recent conversation")
    st.markdown('<div class="chat-container">', unsafe_allow_html=True)

    for msg in st.session_state.chat_history[-10:]:
        role_label = "🧑⚕️ You" if msg["role"] == "user" else "🤖 Assistant"
        bubble_class = "chat-bubble-user" if msg["role"] == "user" else "chat-bubble-assistant"

        st.markdown(
            f"""
            <div class="chat-meta">{role_label}</div>
            <div class="{bubble_class}">{msg["content"]}</div>
            """,
            unsafe_allow_html=True,
        )

    st.markdown("</div>", unsafe_allow_html=True)

    # 7) Sources section under the chat
    st.markdown(
        '<div style="background:#f1f3f4;padding:1rem;border-radius:5px;margin-top:1rem;">',
        unsafe_allow_html=True,
    )
    st.markdown("### 📚 Sources")
    for d in docs:
        st.markdown(f"- {d.metadata['source']}")
    st.markdown("</div>", unsafe_allow_html=True)

def ensure_dir(path: str):
    os.makedirs(path, exist_ok=True)


def file_hash(path: str) -> str:
    h = hashlib.md5()
    with open(path, "rb") as f:
        for chunk in iter(lambda: f.read(4096), b""):
            h.update(chunk)
    return h.hexdigest()


# --------------------------------------------------------
# OCR & Extraction
# --------------------------------------------------------


def azure_ocr(image_bytes: bytes) -> str:
    analyze_url = AZURE_ENDPOINT.rstrip("/") + \
        "/formrecognizer/documentModels/prebuilt-read:analyze?api-version=2023-07-31-preview"
    headers = {
        "Ocp-Apim-Subscription-Key": AZURE_KEY,
        "Content-Type": "application/octet-stream"
    }
    resp = requests.post(analyze_url, headers=headers, data=image_bytes)
    resp.raise_for_status()
    op_url = resp.headers["operation-location"]
    for _ in range(15):
        result = requests.get(op_url, headers={"Ocp-Apim-Subscription-Key": AZURE_KEY}).json()
        if result.get("status") == "succeeded":
            lines = []
            for page in result["analyzeResult"]["pages"]:
                for line in page["lines"]:
                    lines.append(line["content"])
            return "\n".join(lines)
        time.sleep(2)
    return ""


def tesseract_ocr(image_bytes: bytes) -> str:
    img = Image.open(io.BytesIO(image_bytes))
    return pytesseract.image_to_string(img)


def extract_text_from_image(image_bytes: bytes) -> str:
    text = ""
    try:
        text = azure_ocr(image_bytes)
    except Exception as e:
        logger.warning(f"Azure OCR failed: {e}")
    if not text.strip():
        try...

### Answer
Place the if "chat_history" not in st.session_state: block at the very start of main(), right after def main(): and before any other logic (before ensure_dir(...), embeddings test, etc.).

Concretely, change the top of main() to:
def main():
    # initialize chat history once per session
    if "chat_history" not in st.session_state:
        st.session_state.chat_history = []  # list of {"role": "user"/"assistant", "content": str}

    ensure_dir(PDF_DIR)
    ensure_dir(DB_DIR)

    # ✅ Test embedding model dimension (runs once at startup)
    embeddings = HuggingFaceEmbeddings(
        model_name=EMBED_MODEL,
        model_kwargs={"device": "cpu"}
    )
    test_vec = embeddings.embed_query("test")
    logger.info(f"✅ Embedding model: {EMBED_MODEL}, dimension: {len(test_vec)}")

    # (rest of your main() code...)

Make sure the large if query and search: block also stays inside main() (indented to the same level as the rest of its body), not at the global level, and that calculator_section() is still called inside main() near the end.
